[2025-12-29T16:43:21Z] Ryan Cola├зo: X originated in Old English as a term meaning teaching or instruction. In medieval England, it was commonly used to refer to learned knowledge, tradition, or doctrine-especially what was formally taught or *upheld by* *authority* . Over time, its meaning shifted away from  institutional instruction toward knowledge passed down informally, often through oral tradition. As education systems and language evolved, X fell into relative obscurity as a standalone everyday word in spoken English. However, it survived strongly within compound terms-most notably Y-X. In an age when written records focused almost entirely on kings and religious leaders, Y-X came to describe the customs and shared recounting of traditions among ordinary people.
